<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Uganda" title="Politics of Uganda">Politics of Uganda</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Uganda" title="President of Uganda">President of Uganda</a> is both <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. The president appoints a vice-president and a <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Uganda" title="Prime Minister of Uganda">prime minister</a> to aid him in governing.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BushMuseveniEntebbe2003.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="384" data-file-width="514" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/BushMuseveniEntebbe2003.jpg/220px-BushMuseveniEntebbe2003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/BushMuseveniEntebbe2003.jpg/330px-BushMuseveniEntebbe2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/BushMuseveniEntebbe2003.jpg/440px-BushMuseveniEntebbe2003.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BushMuseveniEntebbe2003.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
U.S. President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> met with President Yoweri Museveni in Entebbe, Uganda, July 11, 2003.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The parliament is formed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Uganda" title="National Assembly of Uganda">National Assembly</a>, which has 449 members. These include; 290 constituency representatives, 116 district woman representatives, 10 representatives of the Uganda Peoples Defence Forces, 5 representatives of the youth, 5 representatives of workers, 5 representatives of persons with disabilities and 18 ex-official members.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption">Corruption</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Corruption">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a> has rated Uganda's public sector as one of the most corrupt in the world. In 2016, Uganda ranked 151st worst out of 176 and had a score of 25 on a scale from 0 (perceived as most corrupt) to 100 (perceived as clean).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPI_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-CPI-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>'s 2015 Worldwide Governance Indicators ranked Uganda in the worst 12 percentile of all countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">United States Department of State</a>'s 2012 Human Rights Report on Uganda, "The World Bank's most recent Worldwide Governance Indicators reflected corruption was a severe problem" and that "the country annually loses 768.9 billion shillings ($286 million) to corruption."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Uganda_2012_Human_Rights_Report_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-Uganda_2012_Human_Rights_Report-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ugandan parliamentarians in 2014 were earning 60 times what was being earned by most state employees and they were seeking a major increase. This was causing widespread criticism and protests, including the smuggling of two piglets into the parliament in June 2014 to highlight corruption amongst members of parliament. The protesters, who were arrested, were using the word "MPigs" to highlight their grievance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UganadaMPs_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-UganadaMPs-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>A specific scandal, which had significant international consequences and highlighted the presence of corruption in high-level government offices, was the embezzlement of $12.6 million of donor funds from the Office of the Prime Minister in 2012. These funds were "earmarked as crucial support for rebuilding northern Uganda, ravaged by a 20-year war, and Karamoja, Uganda's poorest region." This scandal prompted the EU, the UK, Germany, Denmark, Ireland, and Norway to suspend aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Widespread grand and petty corruption involving public officials and political patronage systems have also seriously affected the investment climate in Uganda. One of the high corruption risk areas is the public procurement in which non-transparent under-the-table cash payments are often demanded from procurement officers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>What may ultimately compound this problem is the availability of oil. The Petroleum Bill, passed by parliament in 2012 and touted by the NRM as bringing transparency to the oil sector, has failed to please domestic and international political commentators and economists. For instance, Angelo Izama, a Ugandan energy analyst at the US-based Open Society Foundation said the new law was tantamount to "handing over an ATM (cash) machine" to Museveni and his regime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> According to Global Witness in 2012, a non-governmental organization devoted to international law, Uganda now has "oil reserves that have the potential to double the government's revenue within six to ten years, worth an estimated" US $2.4 billion per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Non-Governmental Organizations (Amendment) Act, passed in 2006, has stifled the productivity of NGOs through erecting barriers to entry, activity, funding and assembly within the sector. Burdensome and corrupt registration procedures (i.e. requiring recommendations from government officials; annual re-registration), unreasonable regulation of operations (i.e. requiring government notification prior to making contact with individuals in NGO's area of interest), and the precondition that all foreign funds be passed through the Bank of Uganda, among other things, are severely limiting the output of the NGO sector. Furthermore, the sector's freedom of speech has been continually infringed upon through the use of intimidation, and the recent Public Order Management Bill (severely limiting freedom of assembly) will only add to the government's stockpile of ammunition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_divisions">Political divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Political divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Uganda" title="Administrative divisions of Uganda">Administrative divisions of Uganda</a></div>
<p>Uganda is divided into 112 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Uganda" title="Districts of Uganda">districts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-district_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-district-69">[69]</a></sup> The districts are subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_Uganda" title="Counties of Uganda">counties</a>. Each county is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Sub-counties_of_Uganda" title="Sub-counties of Uganda">sub-counties</a>, parishes, and villages.</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption>Administrative units (August 2014)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-70">[70]</a></sup></caption>
<tr>
<th>Districts</th>
<th>112</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Counties</td>
<td>181</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Sub counties</td>
<td>1,382</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Municipalities</td>
<td>22</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Town councils</td>
<td>174</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Political subdivisions in Uganda are officially served and united by the <a href="/wiki/Uganda_Local_Governments_Association" title="Uganda Local Governments Association">Uganda Local Governments Association</a> (ULGA), a voluntary and non-profit body which also serves as a forum for support and guidance for Ugandan sub-national governments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Parallel with the state administration, five traditional <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a> kingdoms have remained, enjoying some degrees of mainly cultural autonomy. The kingdoms are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toro_Kingdom" title="Toro Kingdom">Toro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Busoga" title="Busoga">Busoga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bunyoro" title="Bunyoro">Bunyoro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buganda" title="Buganda">Buganda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rwenzururu" title="Rwenzururu">Rwenzururu</a>. Furthermore, some groups attempt to restore <a href="/wiki/Ankole" title="Ankole">Ankole</a> as one of the officially recognised traditional kingdoms, to no avail yet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Several other kingdoms and chiefdoms are officially recognized by the government, including the union of Alur chiefdoms, the Iteso paramount chieftaincy, the paramount chieftaincy of Lango and the Padhola state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations_and_military">Foreign relations and military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Foreign relations and military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Uganda" title="Foreign relations of Uganda">Foreign relations of Uganda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uganda_People%27s_Defence_Force" title="Uganda People's Defence Force">Uganda People's Defence Force</a></div>
<p>In Uganda, the <a href="/wiki/Uganda_People%27s_Defence_Force" title="Uganda People's Defence Force">Uganda People's Defence Force</a> serves as the military. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_military_and_paramilitary_personnel" title="List of countries by number of military and paramilitary personnel">number of military personnel in Uganda</a> is estimated at 45,000 soldiers on active duty. The Uganda army is involved in several peacekeeping and combat missions in the region, with commentators noting that only the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">United States Armed Forces</a> is deployed in more countries. Uganda has soldiers deployed in the northern and eastern areas of the Democratic Republic of the Congo and in the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="International_Organization_Memberships">International Organization Memberships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: International Organization Memberships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organization_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organization of Islamic Cooperation">Organization of Islamic Cooperation</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oicmems_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-oicmems-75">[75]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Uganda" title="Human rights in Uganda">Human rights in Uganda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gulu_women_-_cut_lips.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="680" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Gulu_women_-_cut_lips.jpg/250px-Gulu_women_-_cut_lips.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Gulu_women_-_cut_lips.jpg/375px-Gulu_women_-_cut_lips.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Gulu_women_-_cut_lips.jpg/500px-Gulu_women_-_cut_lips.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gulu_women_-_cut_lips.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Two women in <a href="/wiki/Gulu" title="Gulu">Gulu</a> whose lips have been cut off by <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Resistance_Army" title="Lord's Resistance Army">Lord's Resistance Army</a> rebels</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are many areas which continue to attract concern when it comes to human rights in Uganda.</p>
<p>Conflict in the northern parts of the country continues to generate reports of abuses by both the rebel <a href="/wiki/Lord%27s_Resistance_Army" title="Lord's Resistance Army">Lord's Resistance Army</a> (LRA), led by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kony" title="Joseph Kony">Joseph Kony</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Uganda_People%27s_Defence_Force" title="Uganda People's Defence Force">Ugandan Army</a>. A UN official accused the LRA in February 2009 of "appalling brutality" in the Democratic Republic of Congo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>The number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_persons" title="Internally displaced persons">internally displaced persons</a> is estimated at 1.4 million. Torture continues to be a widespread practice amongst security organisations. Attacks on political freedom in the country, including the arrest and beating of opposition members of parliament, have led to international criticism, culminating in May 2005 in a decision by the British government to withhold part of its aid to the country. The arrest of the main opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Kizza_Besigye" title="Kizza Besigye">Kizza Besigye</a> and the siege of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=High_Court_(Uganda)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="High Court (Uganda) (page does not exist)">High Court</a> during a hearing of Besigye's case by heavily armed security forces – before the <a href="/wiki/Ugandan_general_election,_2006" title="Ugandan general election, 2006">February 2006 elections</a> – led to condemnation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hrw1_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-hrw1-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Child_labour" title="Child labour">Child labour</a> is common in Uganda. Many child workers are active in agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr.org_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-unhcr.org-78">[78]</a></sup> Children who work on tobacco farms in Uganda are exposed to health hazards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr.org_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-unhcr.org-78">[78]</a></sup> Child domestic servants in Uganda risk <a href="/wiki/Sexual_abuse" title="Sexual abuse">sexual abuse</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr.org_78-2"><a href="#cite_note-unhcr.org-78">[78]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Trafficking_of_children" title="Trafficking of children">Trafficking of children</a> occurs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr.org_78-3"><a href="#cite_note-unhcr.org-78">[78]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">Slavery</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forced_labour" title="Forced labour">forced labour</a> are prohibited by the Ugandan constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unhcr.org_78-4"><a href="#cite_note-unhcr.org-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>The US Committee for Refugees and Immigrants reported several violations of refugee rights in 2007, including forcible deportations by the Ugandan government and violence directed against refugees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>Torture and extrajudicial killings have been a pervasive problem in Uganda in recent years. For instance, according to a 2012 US State Department report, "the African Center for Treatment and Rehabilitation for Torture Victims registered 170 allegations of torture against police, 214 against the UPDF, 1 against military police, 23 against the Special Investigations Unit, 361 against unspecified security personnel, and 24 against prison officials" between January and September 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Uganda_2012_Human_Rights_Report_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-Uganda_2012_Human_Rights_Report-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2009 Museveni refused Kabaka Muwenda Mutebi, the Baganda king, permission to visit some areas of Buganda Kingdom, particularly the Kayunga district. Riots occurred and over 40 people were killed while others remain imprisoned to this date. Furthermore, 9 more people were killed during the April 2011 "Walk to Work" demonstrations. According to the Humans Rights Watch 2013 World Report on Uganda, the government has failed to investigate the killings associated with both of these events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBT_rights">LGBT rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: LGBT rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Uganda" title="LGBT rights in Uganda">LGBT rights in Uganda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill_protest.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="800" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill_protest.jpg/250px-Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill_protest.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill_protest.jpg/375px-Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill_protest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill_protest.jpg/500px-Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill_protest.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill_protest.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Protests in New York City against Uganda's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-Homosexuality_Bill" title="Anti-Homosexuality Bill">Anti-Homosexuality Bill</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2007, a Ugandan newspaper, the <i><a href="/wiki/Red_Pepper_(newspaper)" title="Red Pepper (newspaper)">Red Pepper</a></i>, published a list of allegedly gay men, many of whom suffered harassment as a result.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 9 October 2010, the Ugandan newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone_(Uganda)" title="Rolling Stone (Uganda)">Rolling Stone</a></i> published a front-page article titled "100 Pictures of Uganda's Top Homos Leak" that listed the names, addresses, and photographs of 100 homosexuals alongside a yellow banner that read "Hang Them".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-82">[82]</a></sup> The paper also alleged that homosexuals aimed to <a href="/wiki/Homosexual_recruitment" title="Homosexual recruitment">recruit</a> Ugandan children. This publication attracted international attention and criticism from human rights organisations, such as <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/No_Peace_Without_Justice" title="No Peace Without Justice">No Peace Without Justice</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Lesbian,_Gay,_Bisexual,_Trans_and_Intersex_Association" title="International Lesbian, Gay, Bisexual, Trans and Intersex Association">International Lesbian, Gay, Bisexual, Trans and Intersex Association</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ILGA_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-ILGA-85">[85]</a></sup> According to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gay_rights" title="Gay rights">gay rights</a> activists, many Ugandans have been attacked since the publication.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Independent_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Independent-86">[86]</a></sup> On 27 January 2011, gay rights activist <a href="/wiki/David_Kato" title="David Kato">David Kato</a> was murdered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, the Ugandan parliament considered an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uganda_Anti-Homosexuality_Bill" title="Uganda Anti-Homosexuality Bill">Anti-Homosexuality Bill</a> that would have broadened the criminalisation of homosexuality by introducing the death penalty for people who have previous convictions, or are HIV-positive, and engage in same-sex sexual acts. The bill also included provisions for Ugandans who engage in same-sex sexual relations outside of Uganda, asserting that they may be <a href="/wiki/Extradition" title="Extradition">extradited</a> back to Uganda for punishment, and included penalties for individuals, companies, media organisations, or non-governmental organisations that support legal protection for homosexuality or sodomy. The <a href="/wiki/Private_member%27s_bill" title="Private member's bill">private member's bill</a> was submitted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" title="Member of Parliament">MP</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Bahati" title="David Bahati">David Bahati</a> in Uganda on 14 October 2009, and was believed to have had widespread support in the Uganda parliament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harpers2010_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Harpers2010-88">[88]</a></sup> The hacktivist group Anonymous hacked into Ugandan government websites in protest of the bill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The debate of the bill was delayed in response to global condemnation but was eventually passed on 20 December 2013 and signed by President Yoweri Museveni on 24 February 2014. The death penalty was dropped in the final legislation. The law was widely condemned by the international community. Denmark, the Netherlands, and Sweden said they would withhold aid. The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> on 28 February 2014 said it would postpone a US$90 million loan, while the United States said it was reviewing ties with Uganda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WorldBankPostponesLOan_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-WorldBankPostponesLOan-90">[90]</a></sup> On 1 August 2014, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Uganda" title="Constitutional Court of Uganda">Constitutional Court of Uganda</a> ruled the bill invalid as it was not passed with the required <a href="/wiki/Quorum" title="Quorum">quorum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> A 13 August 2014 news report said that the Ugandan attorney general had dropped all plans to appeal, per a directive from President Museveni who was concerned about foreign reaction to the bill and who also said that any newly introduced bill should not criminalize same-sex relationships between consenting adults.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_and_infrastructure">Economy and infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy and infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Uganda" title="Economy of Uganda">Economy of Uganda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Uganda" title="Energy in Uganda">Energy in Uganda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Uganda" title="Agriculture in Uganda">Agriculture in Uganda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uganda-Development.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Uganda-Development.JPG/250px-Uganda-Development.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Uganda-Development.JPG/375px-Uganda-Development.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Uganda-Development.JPG/500px-Uganda-Development.JPG 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Uganda-Development.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Downtown <a href="/wiki/Kampala" title="Kampala">Kampala</a>, the capital city.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Uganda" title="Bank of Uganda">Bank of Uganda</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a> of Uganda and handles monetary policy along with the printing of the <a href="/wiki/Ugandan_shilling" title="Ugandan shilling">Ugandan shilling</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, Uganda's economy generated export income from the following merchandise: coffee (US $402.63 million), oil re-exports (US $131.25 million), base metals and products (US $120.00 million), fish (US $117.56 million), maize (US $90.97 million), cement (US $80.13 million), tobacco (US $73.13 million), tea (US $69.94 million), sugar (US $66.43 million), hides and skins (US $62.71 million), cocoa beans (US $55.67 million), beans (US $53.88 million), <a href="/wiki/Sesame" title="Sesame">simsim</a> (US $52.20 million), flowers (US $51.44 million), and other products (US $766.77 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>The country has been experiencing consistent economic growth. In fiscal year 2015–16, Uganda recorded gross domestic product growth of 4.6 percent in real terms and 11.6 percent in nominal terms. This compares to 5.0 percent real growth in fiscal year 2014–15.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:vii</sup></p>
<p>The country has largely untapped reserves of both <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crude_oil" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a> and natural gas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oilrush_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-oilrush-98">[98]</a></sup> While agriculture accounted for 56 percent of the economy in 1986, with coffee as its main export, it has now been surpassed by the services sector, which accounted for 52 percent of GDP in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> In the 1950s, the British colonial regime encouraged some 500,000 subsistence farmers to join co-operatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Since 1986, the government (with the support of foreign countries and international agencies) has acted to rehabilitate an economy devastated during the regime of Idi Amin and the subsequent civil war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kampala_26.08.2009_12-52-00.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2641" data-file-width="3975" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Kampala_26.08.2009_12-52-00.jpg/250px-Kampala_26.08.2009_12-52-00.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Kampala_26.08.2009_12-52-00.jpg/375px-Kampala_26.08.2009_12-52-00.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Kampala_26.08.2009_12-52-00.jpg/500px-Kampala_26.08.2009_12-52-00.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kampala_26.08.2009_12-52-00.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Suburban Kampala.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uganda_Export_Treemap.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="751" data-file-width="960" height="274" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Uganda_Export_Treemap.png/350px-Uganda_Export_Treemap.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Uganda_Export_Treemap.png/525px-Uganda_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Uganda_Export_Treemap.png/700px-Uganda_Export_Treemap.png 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Uganda_Export_Treemap.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Graphical depiction of Uganda's product exports in 28 color-coded categories.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uganda_GV5_lo_(4108162183).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="664" data-file-width="1000" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Uganda_GV5_lo_%284108162183%29.jpg/200px-Uganda_GV5_lo_%284108162183%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Uganda_GV5_lo_%284108162183%29.jpg/300px-Uganda_GV5_lo_%284108162183%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Uganda_GV5_lo_%284108162183%29.jpg/400px-Uganda_GV5_lo_%284108162183%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Uganda_GV5_lo_(4108162183).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Coffee fields in southwestern Uganda</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2012, the World Bank still listed Uganda on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heavily_Indebted_Poor_Countries" title="Heavily Indebted Poor Countries">Heavily Indebted Poor Countries</a> list.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>Economic growth has not always led to <a href="/wiki/Poverty_reduction" title="Poverty reduction">poverty reduction</a>. Despite an average annual growth of 2.5 percent between 2000 and 2003, poverty levels increased by 3.8 percent during that time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-ODI-102">[102]</a></sup> This has highlighted the importance of avoiding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jobless_growth" title="Jobless growth">jobless growth</a> and is part of the rising awareness in development circles of the need for <a href="/wiki/Development_economics#equitable_growth" title="Development economics">equitable growth</a> not just in Uganda, but across the developing world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-ODI-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the Uganda securities exchanges established in 1996, several equities have been listed. The government has used the stock market as an avenue for privatisation. All government treasury issues are listed on the securities exchange. The Capital Markets Authority has licensed 18 brokers, asset managers, and investment advisors including: African Alliance Investment Bank, Baroda Capital Markets Uganda Limited, Crane Financial Services Uganda Limited, Crested Stocks and Securities Limited, Dyer &amp; Blair Investment Bank, Equity Stock Brokers Uganda Limited, Renaissance Capital Investment Bank and UAP Financial Services Limited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> As one of the ways of increasing formal domestic savings, pension sector reform is the centre of attention (2007).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>Uganda traditionally depends on Kenya for access to the Indian Ocean port of <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a>. Efforts have intensified to establish a second access route to the sea via the lakeside ports of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bukasa" title="Bukasa">Bukasa</a> in Uganda and <a href="/wiki/Musoma" title="Musoma">Musoma</a> in Tanzania, connected by railway to <a href="/wiki/Arusha" title="Arusha">Arusha</a> in the Tanzanian interior and to the port of <a href="/wiki/Tanga,_Tanzania" title="Tanga, Tanzania">Tanga</a> on the Indian Ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>Uganda is a member of the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a> and a potential member of the planned <a href="/wiki/East_African_Federation" title="East African Federation">East African Federation</a>.</p>
<p>Uganda has a large diaspora, residing mainly in the United States and the United Kingdom. This diaspora has contributed enormously to Uganda's economic growth through remittances and other investments (especially property). According to the World Bank, Uganda received in 2016 an estimated US $1.099 billion in remittances from abroad, second only to Kenya (US $1.574 billion) in the East African Community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Uganda also serves as an economic hub for a number of neighbouring countries like the Democratic Republic of the Congo,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> South Sudan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> and Rwanda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Ugandan Bureau of Statistics announced inflation was 4.6 percent in November 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poverty">Poverty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Poverty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kampala_26.08.2009_12-39-51.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2697" data-file-width="4063" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Kampala_26.08.2009_12-39-51.jpg/250px-Kampala_26.08.2009_12-39-51.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Kampala_26.08.2009_12-39-51.jpg/375px-Kampala_26.08.2009_12-39-51.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Kampala_26.08.2009_12-39-51.jpg/500px-Kampala_26.08.2009_12-39-51.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kampala_26.08.2009_12-39-51.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Street views in Kampala</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Uganda is one of the poorest nations in the world. In 2012, 37.8 percent of the population lived on less than $1.25 a day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Despite making enormous progress in reducing the countrywide poverty incidence from 56 percent of the population in 1992 to 24.5 percent in 2009, poverty remains deep-rooted in the country's rural areas, which are home to 84 percent of Ugandans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>People in rural areas of Uganda depend on farming as the main source of income and 90 per cent of all rural women work in the agricultural sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> In addition to agricultural work, rural women are responsible for the caretaking of their families. The average Ugandan woman spends 9 hours a day on domestic tasks, such as preparing food and clothing, fetching water and firewood, and caring for the elderly, the sick as well as orphans. As such, women on average work longer hours than men, between 12 and 18 hours per day, with a mean of 15 hours, as compared to men, who work between 8 and 10 hours a day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>To supplement their income, rural women may engage in small-scale entrepreneurial activities such as rearing and selling local breeds of animals. Nonetheless, because of their heavy workload, they have little time for these income-generating activities. The poor cannot support their children at school and in most cases, girls drop out of school to help out in domestic work or to get married. Other girls engage in sex work. As a result, young women tend to have older and more sexually experienced partners and this puts women at a disproportionate risk of getting affected by HIV, accounting for about 57 per cent of all adults living with HIV in Uganda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>Maternal health in rural Uganda lags behind national policy targets and the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goals" title="Millennium Development Goals">Millennium Development Goals</a>, with geographical inaccessibility, lack of transport and financial burdens identified as key demand-side constraints to accessing maternal health services;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> as such, interventions like intermediate transport mechanisms have been adopted as a means to improve women's access to maternal health care services in rural regions of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>Gender inequality is the main hindrance to reducing women's poverty. Women are subjected to an overall lower social status than men. For many women, this reduces their power to act independently, participate in community life, become educated and escape reliance upon abusive men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uganda_-_ad_on_van_in_Kampala.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Uganda_-_ad_on_van_in_Kampala.jpg/250px-Uganda_-_ad_on_van_in_Kampala.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Uganda_-_ad_on_van_in_Kampala.jpg/375px-Uganda_-_ad_on_van_in_Kampala.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Uganda_-_ad_on_van_in_Kampala.jpg/500px-Uganda_-_ad_on_van_in_Kampala.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>

<p>There are seven telecommunications companies serving over 21 million subscribers<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-120">[120]</a></sup> in a population of over 34 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-70">[70]</a></sup> More than 95 percent of internet connections are made using mobile phones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>The total mobile and fixed telephony subscriptions increased from over 20 million to over 21 million yielding an increment of over 1.1 million subscribers (5.4 increase) compared to the 4.1 percent increases realized in the previous quarter Q4 2014 (October–December).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-120">[120]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Uganda" title="Energy in Uganda">Energy in Uganda</a></div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(January 2013)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In the 1980s, the majority of energy in Uganda came from charcoal and wood. However, oil was found in the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Albert_(Africa)" title="Lake Albert (Africa)">Lake Albert</a> area, totaling an estimated 95,000,000 m<sup>3</sup> (3.354893339<span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">×</span>10<sup>9</sup> cu ft) barrels of crude.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oilrush_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-oilrush-98">[98]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Heritage_Oil" title="Heritage Oil">Heritage Oil</a> discovered one of the largest crude oil finds in Uganda, and continues operations there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Water supply and sanitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Uganda" title="Water supply and sanitation in Uganda">Water supply and sanitation in Uganda</a></div>
<p>According to a 2006 published report, the Ugandan water supply and sanitation sector had made substantial progress in urban areas since the mid-1990s, with substantial increases in coverage as well as in operational and commercial performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mugisha_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mugisha-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:3–4</sup> Sector reforms in the period 1998–2003 included the commercialization and modernization of the <a href="/wiki/National_Water_and_Sewerage_Corporation" title="National Water and Sewerage Corporation">National Water and Sewerage Corporation</a> operating in cities and larger towns, as well as decentralization and private sector participation in small towns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:15</sup></p>
<p>Although, these reforms have attracted significant international attention, 38 percent of the population still had no access to an <a href="/wiki/Improved_water_source" title="Improved water source">improved water source</a> in 2010. Concerning access to <a href="/wiki/Improved_sanitation" title="Improved sanitation">improved sanitation</a>, figures have varied widely. According to government figures, it was 70 percent in rural areas and 81 percent in urban areas in 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SPR_2011_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-SPR_2011-125">[125]</a></sup> while according to UN figures it was only 34 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JMP_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-JMP-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>The water and sanitation sector was recognized as a key area under the 2004 Poverty Eradication Action Plan (PEAP), Uganda's main strategy paper to fight poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PEAP_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-PEAP-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:182–188</sup> According to a 2006 published report, a comprehensive expenditure framework had been introduced to coordinate financial support by external donors, the national government, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NGO" title="NGO">nongovernmental organizations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWE_SWAP_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-MWE_SWAP-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:5</sup> The PEAP estimated that from 2001 to 2015, about US $1.4 billion, or US $92 million per year, was needed to increase water supply coverage up to 95 percent, with rural areas needing US $956 million, urban areas and large towns needing US $281 million, and small towns needing US $136 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PEAP_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-PEAP-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:182–183</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Uganda" title="Education in Uganda">Education in Uganda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uganda_students.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2176" data-file-width="3264" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Uganda_students.jpg/250px-Uganda_students.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Uganda_students.jpg/375px-Uganda_students.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Uganda_students.jpg/500px-Uganda_students.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Uganda_students.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Students in Uganda</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_usaid.africa_-_Education_programs_bring_primary_education_to_vulnerable_and_conflict-affected_children_in_Uganda.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1365" data-file-width="2048" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Flickr_-_usaid.africa_-_Education_programs_bring_primary_education_to_vulnerable_and_conflict-affected_children_in_Uganda.jpg/250px-Flickr_-_usaid.africa_-_Education_programs_bring_primary_education_to_vulnerable_and_conflict-affected_children_in_Uganda.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Flickr_-_usaid.africa_-_Education_programs_bring_primary_education_to_vulnerable_and_conflict-affected_children_in_Uganda.jpg/375px-Flickr_-_usaid.africa_-_Education_programs_bring_primary_education_to_vulnerable_and_conflict-affected_children_in_Uganda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Flickr_-_usaid.africa_-_Education_programs_bring_primary_education_to_vulnerable_and_conflict-affected_children_in_Uganda.jpg/500px-Flickr_-_usaid.africa_-_Education_programs_bring_primary_education_to_vulnerable_and_conflict-affected_children_in_Uganda.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_usaid.africa_-_Education_programs_bring_primary_education_to_vulnerable_and_conflict-affected_children_in_Uganda.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Children attending a primary education program for conflict-affected students</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the 2002 census, Uganda had a <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate of 66.8 percent (76.8 percent male and 57.7 percent female).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup> Public spending on education was at 5.2 percent of the 2002–2005 GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Uganda" title="Health in Uganda">Health in Uganda</a> and <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Uganda" title="HIV/AIDS in Uganda">HIV/AIDS in Uganda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lira_Uganda_2010_01_04.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Lira_Uganda_2010_01_04.JPG/250px-Lira_Uganda_2010_01_04.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Lira_Uganda_2010_01_04.JPG/375px-Lira_Uganda_2010_01_04.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Lira_Uganda_2010_01_04.JPG/500px-Lira_Uganda_2010_01_04.JPG 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lira_Uganda_2010_01_04.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Lira,_Uganda" title="Lira, Uganda">Lira, Uganda</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Uganda has been among the rare <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a> success stories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-129">[129]</a></sup> Infection rates of 30 per cent of the population in the 1980s fell to 6.4 percent by the end of 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> However, there has been a spike in recent years compared to the mid-1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the practice of abstinence was found to have decreased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>The prevalence of <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a> (FGM) is low: according to a 2013 UNICEF report,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNICEF2013p27_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNICEF2013p27-133">[133]</a></sup> Only 1 percent of women in Uganda have undergone FGM, with the practice being illegal in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> at birth was estimated to be 53.45 years in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a> rate was approximately 61 deaths per 1,000 children in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> There were eight physicians per 100,000 persons in the early 2000s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_129-2"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-129">[129]</a></sup> The 2006 Uganda Demographic Health Survey (UDHS) indicated that roughly 6,000 women die each year from pregnancy-related complications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> However, recent<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (June 2015)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> pilot studies by Future Health Systems have shown that this rate could be significantly reduced by implementing a voucher scheme for health services and transport to clinics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>Uganda's elimination of user fees at state health facilities in 2001 has resulted in an 80 percent increase in visits, with over half of this increase coming from the poorest 20 percent of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-140">[140]</a></sup> This policy has been cited as a key factor in helping Uganda achieve its Millennium Development Goals and as an example of the importance of equity in achieving those goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI_102-2"><a href="#cite_note-ODI-102">[102]</a></sup> Despite this policy, many users are denied care if they do not provide their own medical equipment, as happened in the highly publicised case of Jennifer Anguko.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> Poor communication within hospitals,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> low satisfaction with health services<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> and distance to health service providers undermine the provision of quality health care to people living in Uganda, and particularly for those in poor and elderly-headed households.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pariyo2009_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-pariyo2009-144">[144]</a></sup> The provision of subsidies for poor and rural populations, along with the extension of public private partnerships, have been identified as important provisions to enable vulnerable populations to access health services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pariyo2009_144-1"><a href="#cite_note-pariyo2009-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2012, there was an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ebola" title="Ebola">Ebola</a> outbreak in the <a href="/wiki/Kibaale_District" title="Kibaale District">Kibaale District</a> of the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> On 4 October 2012, the Ministry of Health officially declared the end of the outbreak after at least 16 people had died.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Health Ministry announced on 16 August 2013 that three people had died in northern Uganda from a suspected outbreak of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congo_Crimean_Hemorrhagic_Fever" title="Congo Crimean Hemorrhagic Fever">Congo Crimean Hemorrhagic Fever</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime_and_law_enforcement">Crime and law enforcement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Crime and law enforcement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(January 2013)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In Uganda, the <a href="/wiki/Allied_Democratic_Forces" title="Allied Democratic Forces">Allied Democratic Forces</a> is considered a violent rebel force that opposes the Ugandan government. These rebels are an enemy of the Uganda People's Defence Force and are considered an affiliate of <a href="/wiki/Al-Shabaab_(militant_group)" title="Al-Shabaab (militant group)">Al-Shabaab</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Science and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Uganda" title="Science and technology in Uganda">Science and technology in Uganda</a></div>
<p>The <i>National Science, Technology and Innovation Policy</i> dates from 2009. Its overarching goal is to ‘strengthen national capability to generate, transfer and apply scientific knowledge, skills and technologies that ensure sustainable utilisation of natural resources for the realisation of Uganda’s development objectives.’ The policy precedes Uganda Vision 2040, which was launched in April 2013 to transform ‘Ugandan society from a peasant to a modern and prosperous country within 30 years,’ in the words of the Cabinet. Uganda Vision 2040 vows to strengthen the private sector, improve education and training, modernize infrastructure and the underdeveloped services and agriculture sectors, foster industrialization and promote good governance, among other goals. Potential areas for economic development include oil and gas, tourism, minerals and information and communication technologies (ICTs).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:12_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-:12-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>Research funding climbed between 2008 and 2010 from 0.33% to 0.48% of GDP. Over the same period, the number of researchers doubled (in head counts) from 1 387 to 2 823, according to the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Institute_for_Statistics" title="UNESCO Institute for Statistics">UNESCO Institute for Statistics</a>. This represents a leap from 44 to 83 researchers per million inhabitants over the same period. One in four researchers is a woman. Uganda has been able to manufacture prototype of cars called kiira in which the government invested 70usd. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:12_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-:12-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Uganda" title="Demographics of Uganda">Demographics of Uganda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cultural_celebrations_resumed_with_the_end_of_the_LRA_conflict_in_Northern_Uganda_(7269658432).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2267" data-file-width="3480" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Cultural_celebrations_resumed_with_the_end_of_the_LRA_conflict_in_Northern_Uganda_%287269658432%29.jpg/300px-Cultural_celebrations_resumed_with_the_end_of_the_LRA_conflict_in_Northern_Uganda_%287269658432%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Cultural_celebrations_resumed_with_the_end_of_the_LRA_conflict_in_Northern_Uganda_%287269658432%29.jpg/450px-Cultural_celebrations_resumed_with_the_end_of_the_LRA_conflict_in_Northern_Uganda_%287269658432%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Cultural_celebrations_resumed_with_the_end_of_the_LRA_conflict_in_Northern_Uganda_%287269658432%29.jpg/600px-Cultural_celebrations_resumed_with_the_end_of_the_LRA_conflict_in_Northern_Uganda_%287269658432%29.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cultural_celebrations_resumed_with_the_end_of_the_LRA_conflict_in_Northern_Uganda_(7269658432).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cultural celebrations in Northern Uganda</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The country has a significant overpopulation problem.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> Uganda's population grew from 9.5 million people in 1969 to 34.9 million in 2014. With respect to the last inter-censal period (September 2002), the population increased by 10.6 million people in the past 12 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> Uganda's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Median_age" title="Median age">median age</a> of 15 years is the lowest in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup> Uganda has the fifth highest <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> in the world, at 5.97 children born per woman (2014 estimates).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_3-6"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>There were about 80,000 <a href="/wiki/Indians_in_Uganda" title="Indians in Uganda">Indians in Uganda</a> before Idi Amin required the <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_Asians_from_Uganda" title="Expulsion of Asians from Uganda">expulsion of Ugandan-Asians</a> (mostly of Indian origin) in 1972, which reduced the population to as low as 7,000. Many Indians, however, returned to Uganda after Amin's fall ouster in 1979. Around 90 percent of Ugandan Indians reside in Kampala.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the UNHCR, Uganda hosted over 190,000 refugees in 2013. Most of the latter came from neighbouring countries in the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">African Great Lakes</a> region, namely <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>, the Democratic Republic of the Congo, <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Uganda" title="Languages of Uganda">Languages of Uganda</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Languages_of_Uganda.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="637" data-file-width="600" height="319" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Languages_of_Uganda.png/300px-Languages_of_Uganda.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Languages_of_Uganda.png/450px-Languages_of_Uganda.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/57/Languages_of_Uganda.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Languages_of_Uganda.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An ethnolinguistic map of Uganda</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>, a widely used language throughout the African Great Lakes region, was approved as the country's second official national language in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_.28Amendment.29_Act_2005_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution_.28Amendment.29_Act_2005-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> English was the only official language until the constitution was amended in 2005. Although Swahili has not been favoured by the Bantu-speaking populations of the south and south-west of the country, it is an important <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i> in the northern regions. It is also widely used in the police and military forces, which may be a historical result of the disproportionate recruitment of northerners into the security forces during the colonial period. The status of Swahili has thus alternated with the political group in power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UCLA_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-UCLA-155">[155]</a></sup> For example, Idi Amin, who came from the north-west, declared Swahili to be the national language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Uganda" title="Religion in Uganda">Religion in Uganda</a></div>

<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Laika_ac_Gaddafi_National_Mosque,_Kampala_(6693328097).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Laika_ac_Gaddafi_National_Mosque%2C_Kampala_%286693328097%29.jpg/190px-Laika_ac_Gaddafi_National_Mosque%2C_Kampala_%286693328097%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Laika_ac_Gaddafi_National_Mosque%2C_Kampala_%286693328097%29.jpg/285px-Laika_ac_Gaddafi_National_Mosque%2C_Kampala_%286693328097%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Laika_ac_Gaddafi_National_Mosque%2C_Kampala_%286693328097%29.jpg/380px-Laika_ac_Gaddafi_National_Mosque%2C_Kampala_%286693328097%29.jpg 2x" width="190"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaddafi_National_Mosque" title="Gaddafi National Mosque">Gaddafi National Mosque</a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the 2002 census, Christians made up about 85 percent of Uganda's population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census_2002_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-Census_2002-157">[157]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Uganda" title="Roman Catholicism in Uganda">Roman Catholic Church</a> had the largest number of adherents (41.9 percent), followed by the <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglican</a> <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Uganda" title="Church of Uganda">Church of Uganda</a> (35.9 percent). <a href="/wiki/Adventism" title="Adventism">Adventist</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangelical" title="Evangelical">Evangelical</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostal" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a>, and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> churches claimed most of the remaining Christians, although there was also a tiny <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" title="Eastern Orthodox">Eastern Orthodox</a> community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census_2002_157-1"><a href="#cite_note-Census_2002-157">[157]</a></sup> The next most reported religion of Uganda was <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Uganda" title="Islam in Uganda">Islam</a>, with Muslims representing 12.1 percent of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census_2002_157-2"><a href="#cite_note-Census_2002-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Muslim population is primarily Sunni. There are also minorities who are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shia" title="Shia">Shia</a> (7 percent), <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadiyya</a> (4 percent), and those that are <a href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Muslim" title="Non-denominational Muslim">non-denominational Muslims</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sufi" title="Sufi">Sufi</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pew_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-pew-158">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>The remainder of the population according to the 2002 census followed traditional religions (1.0 percent), Baha'i (0.1 percent), other non-Christian religions (0.7 percent), or had no religious affiliation (0.9 percent).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Census_2002_157-3"><a href="#cite_note-Census_2002-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Northern_Region,_Uganda" title="Northern Region, Uganda">Northern Region</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/West_Nile_sub-region" title="West Nile sub-region">West Nile sub-region</a>, is predominantly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">Catholic</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Iganga_District" title="Iganga District">Iganga District</a> in eastern Uganda has the highest percentage of Muslims. The rest of the country has a mix of religious affiliations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Uganda" title="Culture of Uganda">Culture of Uganda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Uganda" title="Music of Uganda">Music of Uganda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ugandan_cuisine" title="Ugandan cuisine">Ugandan cuisine</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_African_writers_(by_country)#Uganda" title="List of African writers (by country)">List of African writers (by country) § Uganda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ugandans" title="List of Ugandans">List of Ugandans</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uganda_-_Ruwenzori_Mountain_Lady.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3008" data-file-width="2000" height="301" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Uganda_-_Ruwenzori_Mountain_Lady.jpg/200px-Uganda_-_Ruwenzori_Mountain_Lady.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Uganda_-_Ruwenzori_Mountain_Lady.jpg/300px-Uganda_-_Ruwenzori_Mountain_Lady.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Uganda_-_Ruwenzori_Mountain_Lady.jpg/400px-Uganda_-_Ruwenzori_Mountain_Lady.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Uganda_-_Ruwenzori_Mountain_Lady.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Woman in <a href="/wiki/Rwenzori_Mountains" title="Rwenzori Mountains">Ruwenzori</a> – Western Uganda</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Owing to the large number of communities, culture within Uganda is diverse. Many Asians (mostly from India) who were expelled during the regime of Idi Amin have returned to Uganda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The country has an increasingly successful <a href="/wiki/Uganda_national_basketball_team" title="Uganda national basketball team">national basketball team</a>. It is nicknamed "The Silverbacks",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> and made its debut at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2015_FIBA_Africa_Championship" title="2015 FIBA Africa Championship">2015 FIBA Africa Championship</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Baseball">Baseball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Baseball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In July 2011, Kampala, Uganda qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2011_Little_League_World_Series" title="2011 Little League World Series">2011 Little League World Series</a> in <a href="/wiki/Williamsport,_Pennsylvania" title="Williamsport, Pennsylvania">Williamsport, Pennsylvania</a> for the first time, beating Saudi Arabian baseball team Dharan LL, although visa complications prevented them from attending the series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> Little League teams from Uganda qualified for and attended the <a href="/wiki/2012_Little_League_World_Series" title="2012 Little League World Series">2012</a>.d<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_of_Uganda" title="Media of Uganda">Media of Uganda</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uganda&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Uganda" title="Cinema of Uganda">Cinema of Uganda</a></div>
<p>The Ugandan film industry is relatively young. It is developing quickly, but still faces an assortment of challenges. There has been support for the industry as seen in the proliferation of film festivals such as Amakula, <a href="/wiki/Pearl_International_Film_Festival" title="Pearl International Film Festival">Pearl International Film Festival</a>, Maisha African Film Festival and Manya Human Rights Festival. However filmmakers struggle against the competing markets from other countries on the continent such as those in Nigeria and South Africa in addition to the big budget films from Hollywood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cannesvupar.com_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-cannesvupar.com-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first publicly recognised film that was produced solely by Ugandans was <i>Feelings Struggle</i>, which was directed and written by Hajji <a href="/wiki/Ashraf_Ssemwogerere" title="Ashraf Ssemwogerere">Ashraf Ssemwogerere</a> in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> This marks the year of ascent of film in Uganda, a time where many enthusiasts were proud to classify themselves as cinematographers in varied capacities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-monitor.co.ug_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-monitor.co.ug-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<p>The local film industry is polarised between two types of filmmakers. The first are filmmakers who use the <a href="/wiki/Nollywood" title="Nollywood">Nollywood</a> <a href="/wiki/Video_film_era" title="Video film era">video film era</a>'s guerrilla approach to film making, churning out a picture in around two weeks and screening it in makeshift video halls. The second is the filmmaker who has the film aesthetic, but with limited funds has to depend on the competitive scramble for donor cash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cannesvupar.com_165-1"><a href="#cite_note-cannesvupar.com-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>Though cinema in Uganda is evolving it still faces major challenges. Along with technical problems such as refining acting and editing skills, there are issues regarding funding and lack of government support and investment. There are no schools in the country dedicated to film, banks do not extend credit to film ventures, and distribution and marketing of movies remains poor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cannesvupar.com_165-2"><a href="#cite_note-cannesvupar.com-165">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-monitor.co.ug_167-1"><a href="#cite_note-monitor.co.ug-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Uganda Communications Commission (UCC) is preparing regulations starting in 2014 that require Ugandan television to broadcast 70 percent Ugandan content and of this, 40 percent to be independent productions. With the emphasis on Ugandan Film and the UCC regulations favouring Ugandan productions for mainstream television, Ugandan film may become more prominent and successful in the near future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-monitor.co.ug_167-2"><a href="#cite_note-monitor.co.ug-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
